                                     989                       SYSDEFN
                                     990              *
                                     991              *  Modification history:
                                     992              *
                                     993              *    7-July-1997 - M. Durket
                                     994              *
                                     995              *        Removed all calls to TOEVENP. WYLBUR should NOT be
                                     996              *        generating parity on data destined for terminals.
                                     997              *        That's the job of the front ends.
                                     998              *
                                     999              *        Added checking in the NET_TALK routines for
                                    1000              *        to detect when we're talking to a RSH daemon,
                                    1001              *        so that we can suppress the leading X'00' or
                                    1002              *        X'01' reply. This is to correct a problem noted
                                    1003              *        by LTM in an email (namely, that the WYLBUR ON <host>
                                    1004              *        command couldn't be used in a Forsythe RPC because the
                                    1005              *        leading null terminated the RPC read in the server and
                                    1006              *        killed the session.
                                    1007              *

0                                  25281  1                ¿þþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþþÜ
                                   25282  1                Ÿ  Check whether or not the path control block to the AMELIA        Ÿ
                                   25283  1                Ÿ  path has any buffers queued due to a prior full queue signal     Ÿ
                                   25284  1                Ÿ  from SUZAN. If this is the case, it can set up a problem         Ÿ
                                   25285  1                Ÿ  situation where the full queue emptied code in the PATH          Ÿ
                                   25286  1                Ÿ  module (PATHSNDQ) starts flushing all the previously delayed     Ÿ
                                   25287  1                Ÿ  buffers over to AMELIA. Because the PATH module is non-specific  Ÿ
                                   25288  1                Ÿ  and doesn't know it's dealing with AMELIA, it can dump more      Ÿ
                                   25289  1                Ÿ  data for one connection than AMELIA can buffer, and AMELIA's     Ÿ
                                   25290  1                Ÿ  attempts to send a TCP_STOP control packet will be ignored       Ÿ
                                   25291  1                Ÿ  because PATHSNDQ doesn't check inbound data before sending as    Ÿ
                                   25292  1                Ÿ  this routine does. AMELIA, its STOP having been ignored then     Ÿ
                                   25293  1                Ÿ  aborts the connection. This was first discovered on DEMS         Ÿ
                                   25294  1                Ÿ  FTP SAVEs to goddard.                                            Ÿ
                                   25295  1                Ÿ                                                                   Ÿ
                                   25296  1                Ÿ  What we'll do here is delay a few seconds if we see that a       Ÿ
                                   25297  1                Ÿ  send queue exists for the AMELIA path.                           Ÿ
                                   25298  1                Ÿ                                                                   Ÿ
                                   25299  1                Ÿ   MPD - 8/24/2000                                                 Ÿ
